text:
I've never made fondant before. This recipe requires patience and cooking spray! I sprayed my bowl and spoon before melting the marshmallows. Before I kneaded the dough, I added some Wilton's food color and greased my hands with plenty of shortening, and re-greased as needed. This ensured the dough didn't stick to my hands, nor did the food coloring. It took a LOT of kneading. You'll think it's never going to form a dough, but be patient. It will. You may have to adjust the amount of powdered sugar, adding more as necessary. I ended up using a 10.5 oz. bag of marshmallows and almost an entire 2 lb. bag of powdered sugar to get a good doughy consistency. I left the fondant in the fridge overnight and just now rolled out a test strip. It's great! Tastes good and easy to use. My stepdaughter kept telling me fondant is too hard to use and I'd never be able to do it. She felt and tasted this stuff and said it's 100 times better than the fondant her friend's mom used! I plan to use small portions at a time and keep the rest in the fridge until I need it. I think that will make it easier to work with.

text:
I have some lessons-learned.  I am not a baker and my daughter begged for a fondant-covered cake for her birthday so I tried it.  My first batch stuck so bad to the plastic wrap that I had to throw most of it away.  Either spray the plastic with cooking spray, or dump it out of your mixer right onto the kneading surface.  I also sprayed my bowl before I put the marshmallows in it in the microwave, they dumped right into my mixer without sticking at all.  I tried to spray my mixer and beater, but it didn't help.  Also, you can't really make black fondant with the recipe as-is.  After my fondant turned gray with half a container of black color gel, I realized I had to add cocoa powder first to darken it.  I just substituted the cocoa for a cup of the powdered sugar.  It got a bit dry, so I added another tablespoon of water.

I love this recipe! I will note that it is not a good idea to use a regular hand mixer for this recipe. As soon as I started to blend the marshmallows and water my hand mixer sucked it right up inside of it. Even at the lowest speed. I opted to grease my hands up with Crisco and mixed the sugar in the marshmallow by hands. It is time consuming but it's way better than the butter-cream recipe and not greasy at all. It tastes much better too! It's a lighter recipe for fondant and pairs better with the cake and frosting. Will definitely use again.

BEST fondant recipe EVER!!!  Easy to work with and tastes great!!!  As other review's have said: Use the vegetable shortening instead of the butter - and Wilton's vanilla flavoring instead of pure extract (if you want to keep it *pure* white).  If you are making this on a humid day, then you can dust your surface (and the fondant) with some corn starch.  Works wonders at keeping the fondant a perfect consistency and not too sticky!

Not sure what I did wrong, but this was not easy for me to do. After much hand kneading- my mixer wanted no parts of this- I got what I thought was a stiff dough with good color. Wrapped it up for a day in the fridge so I could bake the cakes, and let it thaw for 6 hours. I had difficulty rolling it out, and felt it was too thick.  Tried wax paper with confectioners sugar on it and had better luck. Once on the cake, it did look nice, but tasted so sweet I couldn't continue with the amount of work it was taking me.  I had to wipe off the excess sugar too.  Ditched the whole thing, cakes included and started over.  Maybe just my inexperience, or I messed up somewhere, but the taste made me end my journey.  I would have peeled it off and asked for a dollop of regular icing, how could I ask my guests to eat it? Maybe this just wasn't the right recipe for me.  Maybe I just don't like fondant? Not sure, but definitely gave this one an honest effort, and still failed.  Maybe my sweet tooth just isn't sweet enough.  As an aside- the kids did like their sample :)

Only problems I had was mixing in the food coloring at ne point (my fault, got ahead of myself) and because I stored the cake in the fridge the fondnt was a bit on the chewy side since it hadnt warmed throughly.

text:
Very good fondant recipe.  Good flavor and less armor-like than other fondants I've had when finished.  As a word of warning, it's very, very sticky until it's been well refrigerated.  I plan to try adding the butter exclusively by buttering my hands repeated next time rather than being in a hurry and trying to knead the butter in quickly but...  No surprise that it's sticky - it is a fondant after all - but make sure you have someone available to answer the phone, hand you tools, etc. as you wouldn't be able to put anything back down if you were interrupted whilst making it!

This tasted good.  Tastes like any other fondant I've had.  This was my first time making fondant. Easy ingredients but it was not easy for me to work with.  I kneaded the fondant for like 20 mins and it never became "pliable".  It stayed sticky.  So I added more powdered sugar but couldnt not get it non sticky.  So i just wraped it up and threw it in the fridge thinking that would do the trick.  While it was cold i couldnt work with it.  It became to hard to roll out.  I ended up letting it come to room temp and rolling it out with tons more powdered sugar.  After putting it on my cake I couldnt not dust off the powdered sugar.  Im sure there must be tricks to making this stuff but it didnt work out for me.  I will prolly make it again after more research on how to get it just right.  It was fun to try something new but im definitly no professional ;)

Worked great, even for a first-time fondant user. I DID notice I had to use more than 2lbs of powdered sugar-- but I also noticed that a standard size mini-marshmallow bag is only 10.5 ounces, not 16. I used a 16oz bag of larger marshmallows, since I thought I needed the whole 16 ounces; but I added probably 2 to 3 more cups of powdered sugar. Maybe if I went with the standard size mini-marsh bag it would have only taken the 2lbs? Either way, the Nintendo cake (see pic 904, at this point) went over with the boy very well. This will be the fondant I use to delve into the brand new world of cake decorating. Thanks, Kiele!

text:
I will never buy fondant again! Just a tip, if you find your fondant too sticky add more icing sugar, if you find it crack when kneading and a bit of shortening does not help, just melt a few more marshmallows add a little bit icing sugar, then mix it with your original cracked fondant. Add icing sugar as needed to bring it back to a workable consistency.

text:
Wow, I have never worked with fondant before, but I have to say this was fairly easy. I decided to melt the marshmallows in a double boiler added the water and  vanilla just as they started to get gooey, and then just added the sugar direct to the hot pan and marshmallows. If you are using food coloring I would suggest making a batch of white first so you can understand the consistency before making food colored batches. The more liquid added the more sugar needed. The hints about adding color to the melted marshmallows rather then kneading it in were great. Also, Crisco THICK on the table with powdered sugar keeps it from sticking when rolling out and lets you get it on the cake very easily.

This was grrrreat! I'm supposda say frugal but I'll be the first to say I'm CHEAP! My sister wanted me to help make my niece's birthday cake and wanted me to bring the fondant. Ha! I one upped her. Found this recipe- that used everything that I already had in my kitchen...and better than that I had marshmallow fluff to boot! I did what another user suggested and refrigerated the fluff overnight (2-7oz containers), sprayed the Kitchenaide bowl, used hook attachment, threw in fluff, I wasn't thinking and threw in whole 2 LB bag of powdered sugar instead of adding a bit at a time, not a problem with a lot of pulsing it pulled together nicely, removed from bowl, kneaded a bit, then rolled out! Might even sound worse than it actually was. Everyone loved the taste. I guess I would describe it kinda circus peanut like. Colored well and went on great! We will do this again and we will try on cookies. Also- with fluff we didn't add water and we omitted the vanilla- don't think we needed it. So pretty good for first attempt as we decorated cake pretty simply, will be more detailed and use some creativity next time. You cannot go wrong with this. believe me!

text:
AWESOME!!  Never thought I would have so much fun making a cake!  It was so easy to make and easy to work with.  I did not use butter, though.  I put the blended marshmallows, water and vanilla (I used clear) on top of 2 lbs of 10x sugar in my kitchenaid, mixed it as well as I could, then covered my kitchen island with seran wrap, grabbed a handfull of shortening and rubbed it all over the counter and hands, dumped the mixture on top of the island and worked it with my hands till completely smooth (it seemed to help letting it sit and dry up a little while i prepped the island).  Was only sticky for a short time.  The shortening left it smooth and moist enough so it didn't crack when rolled out.  I did wet my hands once or twice when I feared it was a little too dry and that seemed to do the trick.  Everyone went CRAZY over the cake...I did Mickey Mouse Clubhouse.  I used styrofoam for the house and head, paper towel rolls cut up for tubing, and rice crispy treats shaped into the slide and the foot.  I'll see if I can post a picture.  I did cheat and used one of my daughters Mickey dress up gloves so I didn't have to shape one out of rice crispy treats (thought it would be too top heavy).

text:
I used this recipe to cover a 3 tier birthday cake and it worked wonderfully. A warning about mixing though, the fondant gets very thick, it actually burnt out the motor of my mixer even before the last cup of sugar had been added. So unless you have a super powered mixer I would recommend mixing a lot by hand. Also, when rolling it out the dough stuck to the surface when using icing sugar alone, so I greased the surface with butter and then covered with icing sugar and that worked just fine.

text:
I've made this fondant several times and it is excellent to work with. As long as you make sure to grease your hands properly before working with it, color will work into it easily. I am still getting the hang of covering a cake with fondant. Depending on the thickness of your fondant for a particular decoration and the time you let it "dry", this fondant can become almost candy-like when it is completely dry. I've found people "fighting" over the fondant decorations that I've used, and I've had several people say it is the only fondant they've actually WANTED to eat. You can also easily make this chocolate by simply adding cocoa powder to the powdered sugar as you are adding it to the recipe. Excellent recipe!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
This was the first fondant I've ever made and ultimately was successful, but not by following the recipe as written. Initially, I attempted to follow the recipe to the letter (trying to force in nearly all of the confectioner's sugar) but this resulted in such a still ball of fondant that I could barely knead it and gave up trying to soften it up by adding water (Note, I couldn't find a 16 oz bag of mini marshmallows--I think 10.5 oz seems to be the standard size around here), so that's the cause, I'm sure!  My second attempt was much better. I used the 10.5 oz bag of mini marshmallows, heating gradually until smooth, with the water. I began by stirring in confectioner's sugar until the mass in the bowl was too difficult to stir. I then transferred the contents of the bowl to my counter, which was greased with Crisco and covered with powdered sugar. I kneaded more sugar in just until the fondant was no longer sticky, coated with a layer of Crisco, wrapped well. I couldn't wait to try it, so I rolled it out a couple of hours later, using powdered sugar and cornstarch on the counter and corn starch on my (regular) rolling pin. I was very pleased with how easy the fondant was to work with! My little sample cake looked great. Can't wait to use it soon on a birthday cake!   As far as taste, it's far too sweet for me, but a thin layer over frosting isn't too much.

Super easy!  I have never made a fondant before and this was so easy and came out divine!  I did not use a mixer or have to wait until marshmallows cooled.  I put the marshmallows in microwave for about 45 seconds, then stirred them until smooth.  I added in the water, vanilla, and some food coloring.  I mixed it all together with a spatula, and it was so workable!  Then I gradually added the sugar until it wasn't sticky!  So easy!  I am making cupcakes that look like cheeseburgers - this was a simple (tasty) solution to making cheese slices!

text:
I love this stuff! A couple of hints- use a stand mixer (like a KA), and mix this using the paddle on a medium speed. You want to add enough powdered sugar to get the mixture to a taffy like consistency. Spray everything w/ Pam- even the plastic wrap you put the fondant in.  I started to knead it after it's well chilled- this is an important step- don't skip the chilling! I greased my hands very well and worked w/ small amounts of fondant at a time. It tastes awesome- really it does! I had 2 children help me cut out the fondant using cutters- a 3 yr old and a 9 yr old- it was easy for them too! I think the key is patience- if it's not ready to roll out, don't try- you'll just have a mess.

text:
Will definitely make it again. I did half the recipe ans ended up using more powdered sugar and cornstarch till it was a little softer then play-doh. I greased the counter top with Crisco. The butter didnt work well and caused the fondant to stick a lot. Once the fondant was on the cake I put a little corn starch and powder sugar mix on my hand and rubbed it on the cake to take away the shine. I used the exact recipe. I also didnt refrigerate it at all and put it straight on the cake. If the fondant gets dry pop it in the microwave for about 5-8 second and it will soften up. Dont leave it in there long it will liquify!!!

text:
This is my second time making this fondant. It turned out fine the first time, but I decided to make a couple changes this time: (because I found it frustrating doing them in the microwave) I melted large marshmallows on the stove in a pot with butter (as one would making rice krispy snacks) and just as marshmallows we're almost melted I added the water and vanilla extract, as well as some red food colouring. I used a spatula to mix it, stirring continuously as not to burn it and keeping on very low heat.  And because I'm low on confectioners sugar, I added regular fine granulated sugar to the melted marshmallows and stirred until dissolved. Then I put some sifted confectioners sugar in a mixing bowl and made a well, and poured the melted marshmallows in and stirred until the dough formed. As I began kneading I noticed the colour was becoming more pink, so I needed to add colour but didn't want serial killer hands at my sons bday party tomorrow. So I used. Clean pair of rubber gloves (the kind for washing dishes or cleaning) and greased them with butter then added my red food colouring. I actually found it much less sticky than using my hands! So the tip is: wear buttered rubber gloves while kneading! :)

text:
I made this according to the recipe, no changes (rating and reviewing a recipe you didn't even follow is misleading). I had a few problems, one of which I knew would be an issue before I made it.
1. It doesn't specify that the sugar needs to be sifted. A beginner might not know to sift confectioners sugar for most recipes anyway. As I said, I made this exactly as the recipe says, and it does not say to sift it. This resulted in clumps of confectioners sugar that wouldn't mix with the rest of the fondant. You either have to take ages finding and correcting each individual little clump, or you have to be okay with a bumpy fondant (which defeats the esthetic purpose of fondant).
2. I needed to add way more sugar than was called for in order to get it to the "no longer sticky to the touch." Some of this was due to the little clumps of unsifted sugar, but it took way more than what was lost to clumping.
3. Contrary to the instructions, it took longer than ten minutes to get to the "smooth and no longer sticky to the touch" stage of kneading.
4. It's not until you're three quarters of the way through kneading that having buttered hands helps at all. Until you're almost done anyway, no amount of butter is going to keep your hands from getting EXTREMELY sticky. I don't mind the stickiness, it comes with the territory, I just want to give you a heads up that the instruction given to help the issue is useless. Don't bother with the butter.

I put it in as it said and put the water and vanilla, but after stirring it wasn't smooth enough so I put it back again for maybe 20 seconds? Then stirred again and repeated until it wasn't lumpy anymore. I used shortening (generic Crisco) instead of butter as someone mentioned and it turned out great! Everything else I followed the recipe! Once the stickiness went away (the shortening definitely helped with this! Keep recoating your hands with it!) it was very pliable. It made a lot too. I was able to completely cover the cake once with one color (the cake was 9-inch diameter, 2 layers tall) and make several decorations for the top, and I still had a LOT left over. I probably could've covered the cake a few more times with all the fondant it made! Before laying the fondant, I did cut the rounded tops off each layer of cake so it'd be flat. I completely iced the yellow cake in chocolate frosting, and then I laid the fondant. Believe it or not the combination of the traditional yellow/chocolate cake with the marshmallow fondant actually worked really well! Before refrigerating, I divided the fondant and colored each as needed before wrapping up. text:
I made this recipe today for my first attempt with fondant.  I made the fondant in my kitchenaid mixer because I didn't want to kneed the dough for 10 minutes.  Kitchenaids have that great attachment just for that!  So, I made the fondant, colored it in 2 different colors, and all went well... until I rolled it out.  I used powdered sugar on a silicone mat, kind of like flour for bread dough.  This stuff stuck like nothing else.  I didn't know anything would stick to silicone mats, but this stuff did.  I added more powdered sugar, and it stuck.  So, I had a mess of a time.  Until I figured out that the author had specified that you use butter to kneed the dough to keep it from sticking to your hands.  I hadn't added any butter, because I wasn't kneeding it by hand.  I added a little butter, and sure enough, the stuff rolled out like a dream.  It didn't stick, it was easy to handle, and everything went smooth from there.  I am so pleased with this recipe!  I will for sure make it again, I had so much fun making this cake!  Next time, I will have the kitchenaid do the kneeding again, but I will add the 1/4 cup butter to the mix.  Thank you, I love it!

text:
If the marshmallows aren't totally melted, just add the water, vanilla and the powered sugar, one cup at a time. After you get more than half the powdered sugar, let a kitchen aid take care of the rest of the kneading. This will also cut down on the butter/crisco. When you roll out the fondant, use extra powdered sugar and keep checking the board for stickiness; especially if you are rolling out large sheets of fondant.

I've never made fondant and I was not  too keen on the traditional version with glycerin and unflavored gelatin - "specialty items".  This one had such simple ingredients!  Couple of tips:  grease your hands frequently (I used Crisco), even if your hands are covered with goo.  It helps it  come off your hands, so don't panic as I nearly did!  I divided it in half to knead and realized that the batch that sat for a while was a lot easier to work with, so next time I'll let it "rest" before kneading.  Last, I used my Kitchen Aid with the dough hook to mix and it worked great.

text:
I was scared to try fondant for the first time, but it turned out great! Super easy, and I even won a bake-off at work.

A couple things I learned that other newbies like me might find useful:

As some reviewers have mentioned, this is not a pure white fondant. Using clear vanilla extract will help with the off-white color that traditional brown vanilla will impart. Or, skip the vanilla altogether.

Secondly: Do not refrigerate the cake once the fondant is on. If you do, when you remove it from the fridge, it will sweat as it comes up to room temperature and not look as nice, and it may cause any additional decor you've added to your cake to melt/run.

text:
Worked out great, just like everyone said it would! Only problem I had was that my low-budget stand mixer didn't want to deal with the thickness of the dough as it came together, so I ended up kneading the whole thing by hand for about 20 minutes. I even discovered (after I totally forgot to add the coloring while it was liquid) that you can melt it back down to semi-liquid form, mix in the food coloring, then let it harden again in the fridge, and it's none the worse for wear. Great that I won't have to waste the whole batch now, just because I forgot one step. This is super easy and tastes better than any real fondant (but it's still not really delicious, it tasted mostly like powdered sugar and not much else). Would be really good on a cake that's not super sweet itself, since this fondant plus a regular boxed cake was far too sweet, and I LOVE sugar!

text:
4 Tbsp water seems to be too much, ~1.5-2 Tbsp water + 1 tsp vanilla-which should be clear, by the way, if you don't want light creamy-golden-brown fondant-works better, as after making several batches I can declare that 4 Tbsp water requires > 2 lbs sugar. Also recommend sifting sugar prior to mixing. Once you get the ratios right this is a good recipe, just wish I hadn't had to spend so much time experimenting/adjusting liquid volumes and running out of sugar.

text:
This recipe does everything it promises... Looks and acts like fondant but tastes better.  I've used it several times with various extracts for different flavor (almond is especially good but so is vanilla as the recipe directs).  Kneading in additional powdered sugar beyond what the recipe directs makes the fondant easier to work with but also eventually makes it tougher so it depends what kind of texture you want.  I've even frozen this fondant after placing it on top of a cake and it has no adverse effect on texture or flavor though the appearance is shinier (this also seems to work better with added powdered sugar).  Great and flexible recipe.

text:
I have NEVER worked with fondant before, but wanted to try it for my son's birthday cake as I was making a baseball cap.  I too followed the recipe and found that I needed more powdered sugar then what it called for.  I continued to add the sugar until it wasn't sticky.  I agree with the other reviews in saying to USE YOUR KA!!  It worked wonders.  The next day I got it to room temp (about 4 hours) before using it.  Rolling it out was very sticky, so I kept adding sugar but didn't seem to work well.  Then I remembered reading a comment which stated to use crisco on everything.  I rubbed some on my hands and on the rolling pin and WOW it was like magic!  It rolled out very nicely and it was easy to handle.  I put it on my cake and within an hour it was dry and looked like a real baseball hat!!  Thanks for sharing this recipe!

I have never worked with fondant before but decided to give this one a try.  As far as the recipe goes, it is very easy to make and does taste delicious.  The actual working with fondant part was not as easy, it kept ripping apart while I was transferring it to the cake ( I kept my nails short and tried to use my palms instead of fingers, but this didn't seem to matter), so I found the only way to prevent that was to roll it out thicker than I wanted it. I think I just need more experience working with fondant, my criticisms are not exactly about this specific recipe, just fondant itself.  It did look beautiful when I finally got it to work though!

text:
My first time making fondant and I think it went really well! I didn't want to make lots of mallow-covered dishes, so I put the marshmallows in my Kitchenaid mixer bowl and set it in a pot of water on the stove as a make-shift double boiler, holding a lid over it in between stirs to aid in the melting. Then put the bowl on the mixer, mixed with liquids, put it back in water, and mixed again with the sugar. When I was down to about a cup of sugar left, I dumped the fondant onto waxed paper covered in remaining sugar and kneaded from there. Messy, but looks great, tastes good, and much cheaper than store bought!

text:
I have made this recipe 3 times now. It is worth every penny to purchase a Wilton Fondant Cut & Roll mat. This will make it MUCH easier to roll your fondant without it sticking, and gives you more time to leave it rolled out before moving it to the cake (you still need a healthy bit of powdered sugar on your surface) . Also, I didn't have to use any butter or crisco at all once I purchased the fondant mat.  For beginners, don't try to bake and/or decorate the day of the party. Make the cake 2 days ahead, and cover it with ganache, or some other firm frosting, and refridgerate it overnight. This gives you a smooth, crumb-free surface to work with. Then do most of the decorating the day before the party.   Finally, I'm not a fan of the taste of fondant at all, but this one tastes decent, and it sure is fun to work with, it gives the cake a really nice appearance, and the kids love it!

text:
This is my first time making fondant...and it was super easy. I melted the marshmallows in the microwave and then I transfered them to the kitchen aid bowl (coated with shortening). I added the water plus vanilla, and the slowly kept on adding the powdered sugar. I used the flat whisk from the kitchen aid. After I integrated all my powdered sugar I covered my hand with the shortening and starting to knead it. It was super easy to make.  It is in the refrigerator in an air tight ziploc bag ( I close the bag leaving 1/4 of an inch open and put a straw inside to get all the air out of the bag). Love this recipe...SUPER HAPPY!!!!

This is a great start.  My son is allergic to gelatin, so I am always looking for ways to get around it. (Gelatin is in marshmallows but not in marshmallow creme).  So I followed the review from Chef4Six.  The first time it didn't turn out so well.  I tried again and wanted to post my results here.  I used 16 ounces of marshmallow creme.  Like the other review, I left out the water step.  I too mixed it in the KA.  I also mixed in about 1 Tablespoon of Crisco while it was in the mixer.  While kneading it, I probably used about the full quarter cup of Crisco.  My results were pretty close to Wilton Fondant.  Not nearly as stretchy though.  Will play with this recipea little more!

text:
When I first found this recipe an tried it, the result was really good. Over the past few years I have tweaked it and made it, in my opinion, better. At least for my needs. I use this recipe on wedding cakes all the time. Here is what I do: 
Use a stand mixer with the dough hook!! Spray all your bowls, spatulas ect that you sue with non stick cooking spray. Measure out 10 cups mini marshmallows, 1Tblsp clear vanilla extract, 2 Tblsp water into a large microwave bowl. Stir marshmallows to coat with van/water. Microwave until melted. Stir again, then pour into mixing bowl. Slowly add an entire 32oz. bag powdered sugar. Once incorporated, turn mixer on med and mix til smooth. Scrape out onto your work table that has been greased with white shortening. Need a bit more then put into a gallon size zip top bag. Place in fridge for a few hours til cool. Bring to room temp before rolling. Use corn starch to "flour" your surface when ready to cover your cake. If it seems a bit too soft, need in a bit of corn starch or powdered sugar. This recipe is best if it is used on the cake the same day it is made. It tastes SO much better than store bought fondant!

text:
This recipe ive used for both my very first and my second times making fondant. I found it fairly simple, slightly tedious as far as the powdered sugar process. My best advice: always ALWAYS buy an extra bag of powdered sugar, use shortening, not butter, and smear your hands and counter with shortening; I spent about 20 minutes trying to get it off my hands and back into the bowl!  All in all, great recipe. Just a tip, if you want to color it, and youve already rolled it out, it doesnt work so well, so id suggest coloring it while your stirring the marshmallows that are nice and hot, or make a new batch :-)

text:
I didn't use butter in the recipe, instead I COVERED my hands in shortening.  Worked great, and kept the marshmallow from sticking too much.  I also added vanilla flavoring (changed the color a little, but was dying it anyway), which really helped the flavor!    Once the fondant was cool, rolling and coloring worked great.  It warms in your hands, so you can always re-work pieces you don't like.  Drying time for me was longer for my 3D pieces, just becuase it was winter and we have a humidifier.  Definately things to consider when starting such a project!

text:
I made this fondant twice in early October (minus the vanilla extract).  The first time I made it was for a practice cake, I kneaded it by hand, and it took forever but it was good and covered the cake well.  The second time I made it was for the 'final' birthday cake and I used my kitchen aide mixer to incorporate the ingredients.  The final result from the KA was a much smoother, more consistant, easier to work with fondant.  The flavor is great!  Others have commented on the end result not being white white but more of an off white color but ours was not, it was very white and worked perfectly for our cake.  I used wilton food colors to color other portions of the fondant and it turned out beautifully!  My daughter LOVED her birthday cake, and so did all of her party guests!!

text:
Ive always bought the prepackaged fondant from the cake supply store and the guy their gave me this recipe. I used it for my last cake and it tastes sooooo much better than the other stuff. It tastes just like chewy marshmallows. And if you get a good enough crumb coat it becomes one with the buttercream and it tastes really yummy together. You can flavor it however you like. I used a bit of coconut oil and it was great with my straw-banana cake. It takes some kneading to get the sugar in but the prepackaged stuff takes some kneading as well so it evens out in the end. Plus compared to the pricey store bought stuff you simply cant go wrong. It literally costs me 75% less and the ingredients are always available. One thing I did change was I only used half of the water and added it to the marshmallows in the microwave and I used white shortening instead of butter. It was super easy!

This turned out very well. My sister makes it as the recipes says and complains of the huge mess left after kneading the dough on the counter. I greased up my stand mixer, threw the remaining butter flavored crisco into the bowl and used the dough hook with great success! I used more powdered sugar than the recipe calls for, but I was going for the right consistency rather than an exact quantity. I will, in the future, try other flavors than vanilla, I think a light maple might be good, or even mint, or almond. Thanks for sharing this great recipe!

text:
I made this fondant 3 times.  The first time came out the best.  It looked great and tasted better than store bought.  I had to use an additional 2 cups of confectioners sugar to get the right consistency.  The second batch was was ok, but there were pock marks when I rolled it out.   It also didn't hold the color.  I used the Wilton gel color and after I covered the cake the color started to fade.  2 days later it was white again.  Does anyone know why this may have happened?  My cake looked gorgeous despite this snafu, but I was bummed about the color.
